On Friday, October 31, 2014, Robert Scholte &lt;rfscholte@apache.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; see MRELEASE-165 (release:prepare should fail if the tag already exists)[1]&#010;&gt; The main reason why it is still not implemented, is that this must be&#010;&gt; solved in the SCM project. If we know how to do a valid(!) check of the&#010;&gt; existence of a tag for the scm providers, we could start implementing it.&#010;&#010;&#010;Actually we need only have the SCM api return a tristate:&#010;&#010;Exists&#010;Doesn't exist&#010;Don't know&#010;&#010;Then the default impl can return don't know, and the release plugin can&#010;implement the check via the SCM API immediately... That makes the problem&#010;just belong to the SCM API implementations&#010;&#010;;-)&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; My experience is, is that these kind of issues only happen at the start of&#010;&gt; a new project. Once it works, it'll all stay fine.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; About the rollback: it's already there: release:rollback[2]&#010;&gt; And it works just as you described. However, if you do the release with&#010;&gt; the Jenkins m2-release-plugin, that plugin in still missing the rollback&#010;&gt; option[3].&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; thanks,&#010;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [1] https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MRELEASE-165&#010;&gt; [2] http://maven.apache.org/maven-release/maven-release-plugin/&#010;&gt; rollback-mojo.html&#010;&gt; [3] https://issues.jenkins-ci.org/browse/JENKINS-8038&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Op Fri, 31 Oct 2014 17:26:52 +0100 schreef Bernd Eckenfels &lt;&#010;&gt; ecki@zusammenkunft.net&gt;:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;  Hello,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; one thing which bites me quite regularly with the maven release plugin&#010;&gt;&gt; is the fact, that it will update the POMs to the release version then&#010;&gt;&gt; commit them and then tag them. If the tagging fails (especially because&#010;&gt;&gt; the tag existed already) then it will leave the head on a released&#010;&gt;&gt; version number.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; This is in my case a problem as I have to go through a gerrit release&#010;&gt;&gt; to change it to a snapshot version to try again.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; A good improvement would be to first check the existence of the tag.&#010;&gt;&gt; This would not cover all error cases but the most common.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Another option (or in addition to that), a rollback action would be to&#010;&gt;&gt; actually commit the updated POM with the old snapshot version again?&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; (just to warn people, in my case if an integration build is triggert on&#010;&gt;&gt; the master which has configured jenkins to deploy (normally the&#010;&gt;&gt; snapshots) it will happyly deply the released version).&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Gruss&#010;&gt;&gt; Bernd&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Sent from my phone&#010;&#010;

Some further research on my part shows that a simple connection test&#010;using HttpComponents httpclient 4.3.5 does work, but that the version&#010;of httpclient used in Wagon 2.6 (httpclient 4.3.1) fails. Apparently&#010;the newer version of httpclient fixes the problem I ran into, although&#010;I do not know what the problem is exactly.&#010;&#010;For completeness sake: the simple connection test with httpclient 4.3.5 I used:&#010;https://gist.github.com/jdhoek/192a965fc63f459b2bee&#010;&#010;As it turns out, Wagon 2.7 already uses httpclient 4.3.5. A custom&#010;build of Maven 3.2.3 with the Wagon dependency set to 2.7 works!&#010;&#010;When will a version of Maven 3.2.x built with Wagon 2.7 be released?&#010;&#010;Is something blocking Maven from depending on Wagon 2.7?&#010;&#010;2014-10-29 16:14 GMT+01:00 Jeroen Hoek &lt;jeroen@lable.org&gt;:&#010;&gt; Hello,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I am trying to get Maven (3.2.2) to work with an instance of Archiva&#010;&gt; hosted behind a webserver secured with client-side SSL certificates.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have followed the guide at&#010;&gt; https://maven.apache.org/guides/mini/guide-repository-ssl.html, and&#010;&gt; imported the server-side SSL certificate into a Java .jks file. The&#010;&gt; client-side certificate is a PKCS12 file, which works correctly in&#010;&gt; Firefox and Chromium.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have a simple project that depends on an artifact hosted on my&#010;&gt; Archiva server. When client-side SSL verification is disabled on the&#010;&gt; server, `mvn clean install` works as expected, and the dependency is&#010;&gt; downloaded.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But it doesn't work when I activate client-side SSL verification, and&#010;&gt; try the following command:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; mvn clean install -Djavax.net.debug=ssl&#010;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.trustStore=PATH_TO_TRUSTDB.jks&#010;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.trustStorePassword=****************&#010;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStore=PATH_TO_MY_CERT.p12&#010;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStoreType=pkcs12&#010;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStorePassword=****************&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; From what I can see in the output, my .p12 file is read by Maven at&#010;&gt; the start, as is the trust-store, but it fails to complete requests to&#010;&gt; the Archiva server, although TLS handshaking appears to work, so the&#010;&gt; server-side certificate is trusted and accepted. The server throws the&#010;&gt; "400: No required SSL certificate was sent" error message you get when&#010;&gt; trying to talk to it without a client-side SSL certificate installed.&#010;&gt; In the server log I am indeed seeing HTTP GET requests from Maven&#010;&gt; without any client-side SSL certificate, whereas GETs by a browser do&#010;&gt; show access with the valid certificate there.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Any idea why Maven isn't using the client-side SSL certificate passed&#010;&gt; via -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStoreType? Is there some configuration option I&#010;&gt; am overlooking?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Kind regards,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Jeroen Hoek&#010;&gt; Lable&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Vriendelijke groeten,&#010;&#010;Jeroen Hoek&#010;&#010;Lable&#010;✉ jeroen@lable.org&#010;℡ 088 44 20 202&#010;&#010;http://lable.org&#010;KvK № 55984037&#010;BTW № NL8519.32.411.B.01&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

When client-side SSL verification is disabled on the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; server, `mvn clean install` works as expected, and the dependency is&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; downloaded.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; But it doesn't work when I activate client-side SSL verification, and&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; try the following command:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; mvn clean install -Djavax.net.debug=ssl&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.trustStore=PATH_TO_TRUSTDB.jks&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.trustStorePassword=****************&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStore=PATH_TO_MY_CERT.p12&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStoreType=pkcs12&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStorePassword=****************&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;  From what I can see in the output, my .p12 file is read by Maven at&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; the start, as is the trust-store, but it fails to complete requests to&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; the Archiva server, although TLS handshaking appears to work, so the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; server-side certificate is trusted and accepted. The server throws the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; "400: No required SSL certificate was sent" error message you get when&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; trying to talk to it without a client-side SSL certificate installed.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; In the server log I am indeed seeing HTTP GET requests from Maven&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; without any client-side SSL certificate, whereas GETs by a browser do&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; show access with the valid certificate there.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Any idea why Maven isn't using the client-side SSL certificate passed&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; via -Djavax.net.ssl.keyStoreType? Date  :-
Mon, 03 Nov 2014 01:48:38 GMT  
contents:-

On 3 November 2014 20:07, Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Well I knew I'd written something on that topic... but re-reading I am&#010;&gt; surprised at how much information I managed to cram in there without it&#010;&gt; feeling over dense (for me)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; BTW I am of the *never deploy -SNAPSHOTs* camp but I recognise that there&#010;&gt; are other people out there... and I have to interact with them some times&#010;&gt; and that post is helpful to explain things to them!&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;I think its important for people to try things, because this stuff is&#010;complicated, and unless you get yours hands dirty it is difficult to&#010;understand and get a feel for why it doesn't work.&#010;&#010;After you have been burnt by a dependency being updated from underneath you&#010;- one that you have your own changes in - then you realise that you need to&#010;"build twice" to rebuild the other snapshot to keep going, and that the&#010;other developers haven't gotten their head around the build process and why&#010;things sometimes dont work... It makes life simpler to avoid deploying the&#010;snapshots for developer consumption.&#010;&#010;

Hello,&#010;&#010;Thanks Stephen for that writeup. It is a good read. For my taste it&#010;over-emphasises the moving ground problem. I mean when cooperating with&#010;larger projects and lots of developers you get all kinds of problems, but&#010;beeing affected by breaking changes of updating snapshots - I cant remember&#010;to ever experience that. In fact when SNAPSHOTs change in a severe way it&#010;is most likely that I have waited for it, I manually refreshed the&#010;dependencies and I am actually happy to see the changes as early as&#010;possible (before integrating into a system which isnt working since days&#010;and only my old snapshots hide this from me).&#010;&#010;But having said that, I also do enjoy an environment with releasing often.&#010;This allows each team to decide when to pull in which (released) changes,&#010;and this indeed lowers the frequency of broken builds (however it also&#010;encourages developers to wait too long with the integration, if you dont&#010;nudge them with deoendency upgrade reports).&#010;&#010;Gruss&#010;Bernd&#010;Am 03.11.2014 10:39 schrieb "Stephen Connolly" &lt;&#010;stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; You can overwrite the checkstyle version. My configuration looks like this:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;     &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;     &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-checkstyle-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;     &lt;version&gt;2.12.1&lt;/version&gt;&#010;     &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&lt;configLocation&gt;checkstyle.xml&lt;/configLocation&gt;&#010;&lt;includeTestSourceDirectory&gt;false&lt;/includeTestSourceDirectory&gt;&#010;         &lt;failsOnError&gt;true&lt;/failsOnError&gt;&#010;     &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;     &lt;executions&gt;&#010;         &lt;execution&gt;&#010;             &lt;phase&gt;verify&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;             &lt;goals&gt;&#010;                 &lt;goal&gt;checkstyle&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;             &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;         &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;     &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;     &lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;         &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;             &lt;groupId&gt;com.puppycrawl.tools&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;             &lt;artifactId&gt;checkstyle&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;             &lt;version&gt;5.9&lt;/version&gt;&#010;         &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;     &lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Kind regards,&#010;Joachim&#010;&#010;On 2014-11-03 11:39, Alexander Wessel wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi guys,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I like to use the Apache Maven Checkstyle-Plugin with Java 8 but unfortunately it uses&#010;Checkstyle 5.7 that doesn't support Java 8. Dan Tran &lt;dant...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
[ANN] RPM Maven Plugin version 2.1 - Released  
Date  :-
Mon, 03 Nov 2014 17:33:35 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the RPM Maven Plugin&#010;version 2.1.&#010;&#010;The RPM Maven Plugin allows artifacts from one or more projects to be&#010;packaged in an RPM for distribution. In addition to project artifacts, the&#010;RPM can contain other resources to be installed with the artifacts and&#010;scripts to be run while the package is being installed and removed. This&#010;plugin does not support the full range of features available to RPMs. In&#010;particular, source RPMs can not be generated and the spec files which are&#010;used do not do any build process (the plugin collects the files and&#010;"installs" them for packaging).&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/rpm-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin&#010;configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;rpm-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.1&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes:&#010;*http://jira.codehaus.org/secure/ReleaseNote.jspa?projectId=11970&amp;version=20367&#010;&lt;http://jira.codehaus.org/secure/ReleaseNote.jspa?projectId=11970&amp;version=20367&gt;*&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;Dan Tran&#010;&#010;

The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven Clean Plugin, version 2.6.1&#010;&#010;The Clean Plugin is used when you want to remove files generated at build-time&#010;in a project's directory.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-clean-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-clean-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.6.1&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Clean Plugin - Version 2.6.1&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010; * [MCLEAN-47] - On windows if there are junctions on the cleaned directories, clean deletes&#010;.* resources under junction's target along with junction.&#010; * [MCLEAN-55] - maven clean seems to use old java.io API to clean the target directory&#010; * [MCLEAN-58] - Maven Clean Plugin ignores followSymLinks parameter on Windows&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010; * [MCLEAN-59] - Upgrade maven-plugins-testing-harness from 1.1 to 1.3&#010; * [MCLEAN-60] - Fixed Checkstyle reported errors / warnings&#010; * [MCLEAN-61] - Upgrade to org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-plugins:26&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Paul Benedict &lt;pbened...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: explicit dependencies in maven  
Date  :-
Tue, 04 Nov 2014 04:43:07 GMT  
contents:- 
Your pom.xml should declare all dependency versions explicitly. And to&#010;prevent any changes, do not use any snapshots. Furthermore, use&#010;dependency:analyze on your project to make sure all libraries in use are&#010;explicitly declared. After you lock them all down, tell your developers not&#010;to update the pom.xml file. That will ensure it.&#010;&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Paul&#010;&#010;On Mon, Nov 3, 2014 at 10:33 PM, Irfan Sayed &lt;irfu.sayed@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; hello,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; is there any good doc/blog which describes the handling of explicit&#010;&gt; declaration of dependencies.&#010;&gt; when we build the code, we use certain dependencies , how we can make sure&#010;&gt; that when we reproduce the same build after the gap of 6 months , same and&#010;&gt; exact dependencies will be used. ???&#010;&gt; i know we can have artifactory/nexus , but that does not guarantee the&#010;&gt; exact version of dependency when developer changes the code and make it&#010;&gt; public keeping the version same&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; please suggest&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; regards&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Have you scanned the Maven books referenced on the Maven web site? Best &#010;starting place.&#010;&#010;With a repository (Nexus), people are prevented from deploying the same &#010;version twice so you are guaranteed that if you build with version &#010;2.3.15 of ourNiceUtility, you will always get the same code. The repo &#010;will simply not allow them to overwrite version 2.3.15 once it is &#010;deployed into the wild(public).&#010;&#010;Beats firing developers but stops them from doing silly things.&#010;&#010;&#010;On 03/11/2014 11:33 PM, Irfan Sayed wrote:&#010;&gt; hello,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; is there any good doc/blog which describes the handling of explicit&#010;&gt; declaration of dependencies.&#010;&gt; when we build the code, we use certain dependencies , how we can make sure&#010;&gt; that when we reproduce the same build after the gap of 6 months , same and&#010;&gt; exact dependencies will be used. ???&#010;&gt; i know we can have artifactory/nexus , but that does not guarantee the&#010;&gt; exact version of dependency when developer changes the code and make it&#010;&gt; public keeping the version same&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; please suggest&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; regards&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi,&#010;&#010;to be clear on that point you should never change released versions.&#010;&#010;The idea of releases is that they are immutable.&#010;&#010;The scenario you have described should never be done which means:&#010;&#010;If you change code than make simply a new version like 1.2 or may be &#010;better things like 1.1.1 to show it's a bug fix release of 1.1 etc.&#010;&#010;You should prevent of doing developers such a thing...&#010;&#010;Apart&#010;Kind regrards&#010;Karl Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;On 11/4/14 6:06 AM, Irfan Sayed wrote:&#010;&gt; so, lets say if i am using x dependency with version 1.1 and if the&#010;&gt; developer changes the code of that dependency, keeping the same version as&#010;&gt; 1.1&#010;&gt; then nexus will not download the latest code changes for that dependency&#010;&gt; because the version still refers to 1.1 ???&#010;&gt; if that is the case, this is really nice&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; regards&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Tue, Nov 4, 2014 at 10:20 AM, Ron Wheeler &lt;rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Have you scanned the Maven books referenced on the Maven web site? Best&#010;&gt;&gt; starting place.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; With a repository (Nexus), people are prevented from deploying the same&#010;&gt;&gt; version twice so you are guaranteed that if you build with version 2.3.15&#010;&gt;&gt; of ourNiceUtility, you will always get the same code. The repo will simply&#010;&gt;&gt; not allow them to overwrite version 2.3.15 once it is deployed into the&#010;&gt;&gt; wild(public).&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Beats firing developers but stops them from doing silly things.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On 03/11/2014 11:33 PM, Irfan Sayed wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; hello,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; is there any good doc/blog which describes the handling of explicit&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; declaration of dependencies.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; when we build the code, we use certain dependencies , how we can make sure&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; that when we reproduce the same build after the gap of 6 months , same and&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; exact dependencies will be used. ???&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; i know we can have artifactory/nexus , but that does not guarantee the&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; exact version of dependency when developer changes the code and make it&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; public keeping the version same&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; please suggest&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; regards&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
Please be aware, changing the code of a released library (not SNAPSHOT) is not allowed and&#010;maven can not take any responsibility for any errors this will cause.&#010;Thats why nexus/artifactory do not allow to change the artifact of a released version once&#010;its uploaded. &#010;Only SNAPSHOT versions are allowed to be changed.&#010;Domi&#010;&#010;On 04.11.2014, at 08:10, Irfan Sayed &lt;irfu.sayed@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; thanks.&#010;&gt; what i figured out is , nexus / artifactory will not download the&#010;&gt; dependency unless there is change in the version.&#010;&gt; if dependency x  refers version 1.1 , then maven will see if&#010;&gt; nexus/artifactory has this version along with local maben repo of build&#010;&gt; machine&#010;&gt; if it does both, maven will not download the dependency even if developer&#010;&gt; changes the code keeping the version same&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; regards&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; On Mon, Oct 20, 2014 at 5:55 AM, Bernd Eckenfels &lt;ecki@zusammenkunft.net&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Hello,&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; I was looking a bit deeper into making the dependency plugin to print&#010;&gt;&gt; out the resolved timestamps. I noticed there is already an option&#010;&gt;&gt; -DoutputAbsoluteArtifactFilename=true which would give me the path of&#010;&gt;&gt; the files in the local directory. On 05/11/2014 1:18 AM, Mirko Friedenhagen wrote:&#010;&gt; And the scheme as I read it is MAJOR.FEATURE_MINOR.SECURITY.PATCHLEVEL and&#010;&gt; FEATURE_MINOR and SECURITY are sort of independent, so a bigger minor might&#010;&gt; be less secure.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards&#010;&gt; Mirko&#010;&#010;I gather that the assumption is that 9.2.20 would include all of the &#010;security patches of 9.1.20 and that one would never issue a 9.2.19 after &#010;9.1.20 had been released and that security bugs would always be released &#010;on the higher versions first.&#010;A release pattern of 9.1.19, 9.2.19 and 9.2.20 followed by a backporting &#010;to 9.1.20 would be expected rather than&#010;9.1.19, 9.2.19, 9.1.20 followed by 9.2.20.&#010;&#010;However, the second release pattern might come about if the 9.2.19 &#010;release is not widely adopted and there is a lot of interest in fixing &#010;the security problem in 9.1.19 since it is in more production &#010;environments or in the environment of the person doing the patching.&#010;&#010;Version numbers in and of themselves do not guarantee security but at &#010;least you can easily see that a 9.2.21 release has at least some &#010;security flaw fixed that 9.2.20 did not but it does not have any added &#010;functionality.&#010;&#010;It also makes it easier to discuss security.&#010;9.x.20 includes fixes security issues 6789,6897, 6899&#010;9.x.21 includes fixes for security issues 6931,6944&#010;&#010;If the security patches are backported, one could easily see that 9.1.21 &#010;and 9.2.21 have the same security patches applied (unless some only &#010;apply to new features in 9.2.20 that do not cause a security problem in &#010;9.1.20).&#010;If none of the security patches in 9.2.21 apply to 9.1.20, does one &#010;still issue a 9.1.21 just to signal that it is just as secure as 9.2.21 &#010;even though none of the x.x.21 patches were applied?&#010;&#010;When security patches apply to different major versions, one has to do a &#010;bit of reading to find out that 8.3.35 (actually 8.x.35) has the same &#010;security patches (at least the ones that apply) as 9.2.21(9.x.21). &#010;Security release 34 in release 8.x.34 is not as secure as 21 in 9.x.21 &#010;but 9.x.21 is just as secure as 8.x.35.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: Subject  :-
[ANN] Animal Sniffer 1.12 Released  
Date  :-
Wed, 05 Nov 2014 10:36:19 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of Animal Sniffer version&#010;1.12.&#010;&#010;Animal Sniffer provides tools to assist verifying that classes&#010;compiled with a newer JDK/API are compatible with an older JDK/API.&#010;&#010;The following tools are provided by animal sniffer:&#010;&#010;* A command line tool to dump the class file version number&#010;(http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer/animal-sniffer/index.html).&#010;This helps you track down the offending jar file when you see&#010;UnsupportedClassVersionError.&#010;&#010;* A set of ANT tasks&#010;(http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer/animal-sniffer-ant-tasks/index.html&#010;)&#010;for verifying that your classes comply with an API signature as well&#010;as tasks for creating API signatures from a JDK, or a collection or&#010;jar and class files, or a collection of other API signature files, or&#010;combination of these elements.&#010;&#010;* A rule for use in the maven-enforcer-plugin&#010;(&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer/animal-sniffer-enforcer-rule/index.html&#010;)&#010;for verifying that your classes comply with an API signature .&#010;&#010;* A maven plugin&#010;(http://mojo.codehaus.org/animal-sniffer-maven-plugin/index.html) for&#010;verifying that your classes comply with an API signature as well as&#010;for creating API signatures from a JDK, or the current module's&#010;classes, or the current module's dependencies, or a collection of&#010;other API signature files, or combination of these elements.&#010;&#010;The artifacts have are available from the Maven Central repository.&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Mojo's Animal Sniffer - Version 1.12&#010;&#010;** New Feature&#010;    * [MANIMALSNIFFER-47] - Allow the maven plugin and enforcer rule to be&#010;able to filter the dependencies&#010;&#010;The Mojo Team.&#010;&#010;

Curtis Rueden &lt;ctrue...@wisc.edu&gt;  
Subject  :-
maven-javadoc-plugin: resource folders interpreted as illegal package names  
Date  :-
Wed, 05 Nov 2014 18:42:44 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi everyone,&#010;&#010;I am trying to generate an aggregated set of javadocs from a collection of&#010;related projects, like so:&#010;&#010;https://github.com/imagej/imagej-javadoc/blob/83d2fe7f2d546cdc0971f323dfaf56d0089e715d/pom.xml&#010;&#010;Basically, this POM project declares a bunch of dependencies and then uses&#010;the maven-javadoc-plugin's&#010;&lt;includeDependencySources&gt;true&lt;/includeDependencySources&gt; option.&#010;&#010;Some of the dependencies have a "script-templates" folder in their&#010;resources, which gets lumped into the "-sources" JAR by the&#010;maven-source-plugin.&#010;&#010;Unfortunately, the javadoc tool hates seeing folders with violate java&#010;package naming conventions. So my build ultimately fails with:&#010;&#010;[ERROR] Failed to execute goal&#010;org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-javadoc-plugin:2.9.1:jar (attach-javadocs)&#010;on project imagej-javadoc: MavenReportException: Error while creating&#010;archive:&#010;[ERROR] Exit code: 1 - javadoc: error - Illegal package name:&#010;"script-templates.Java"&#010;&#010;I tried adding &lt;excludePackageNames&gt;script-templates&lt;/excludePackageNames&gt;&#010;to the maven-javadoc-plugin configuration, but it seemed to have no effect.&#010;&#010;Does anyone have ideas how to work around this problem?&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;P.S. I could rename the "script-templates" folders in all of the&#010;dependencies, and then update the code to handle both the old and new&#010;resource locations, and then release new versions of them all, but that&#010;would be a substantial amount of work. And the problem could still crop up&#010;again later if any other incompatibly-named folders appear in any&#010;"-sources" JARs.&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Curtis Rueden &lt;ctrue...@wisc.edu&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: maven-javadoc-plugin: resource folders interpreted as illegal package names  
Date  :-
Thu, 06 Nov 2014 19:29:18 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi all,&#010;&#010;OK, given the deafening silence, I posted it on SO:&#010;http://stackoverflow.com/q/26787825/1207769&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;On Wed, Nov 5, 2014 at 12:42 PM, Curtis Rueden &lt;ctrueden@wisc.edu&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi everyone,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I am trying to generate an aggregated set of javadocs from a collection of&#010;&gt; related projects, like so:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; https://github.com/imagej/imagej-javadoc/blob/83d2fe7f2d546cdc0971f323dfaf56d0089e715d/pom.xml&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Basically, this POM project declares a bunch of dependencies and then uses&#010;&gt; the maven-javadoc-plugin's&#010;&gt; &lt;includeDependencySources&gt;true&lt;/includeDependencySources&gt; option.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Some of the dependencies have a "script-templates" folder in their&#010;&gt; resources, which gets lumped into the "-sources" JAR by the&#010;&gt; maven-source-plugin.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Unfortunately, the javadoc tool hates seeing folders with violate java&#010;&gt; package naming conventions. So my build ultimately fails with:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [ERROR] Failed to execute goal&#010;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-javadoc-plugin:2.9.1:jar (attach-javadocs)&#010;&gt; on project imagej-javadoc: MavenReportException: Error while creating&#010;&gt; archive:&#010;&gt; [ERROR] Exit code: 1 - javadoc: error - Illegal package name:&#010;&gt; "script-templates.Java"&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I tried adding &lt;excludePackageNames&gt;script-templates&lt;/excludePackageNames&gt;&#010;&gt; to the maven-javadoc-plugin configuration, but it seemed to have no effect.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Does anyone have ideas how to work around this problem?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; Curtis&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; P.S. I could rename the "script-templates" folders in all of the&#010;&gt; dependencies, and then update the code to handle both the old and new&#010;&gt; resource locations, and then release new versions of them all, but that&#010;&gt; would be a substantial amount of work. And the problem could still crop up&#010;&gt; again later if any other incompatibly-named folders appear in any&#010;&gt; "-sources" JARs.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the&#010;Apache Maven Assembly Plugin, version 2.5.1.&#010;&#010;The Assembly Plugin for Maven is primarily intended to allow users to aggregate&#010;the project output along with its dependencies, modules, site documentation,&#010;and other files into a single distributable archive.&#010;&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin/&#010;&#010;(Note; there are some problems with clustering/replication on the&#010;apache web servers&#010;and pressing refresh may sometimes give you an old version of the site)&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-assembly-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.5.1&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Assembly Plugin - Version 2.5.1&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-357] - transitive dependencies erroneously excluded&#010;from dependencySet in some cases&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-395] - Module dependencies not included&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-474] - Assembly is duplicating dependecies in the output&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-533] - Outputidrectory appended by dependencyset&#010;include name on filtered=true&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-554] - DependencySet unpackOptions 'filtered' causes&#010;unpack not to work&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-559] - useTransitiveDependencies leaks from one&#010;dependency set to another&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-571] - moduleSet dependencies processed incorrectly&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-577] - dependencySet inside moduleSet/binaries picks&#010;up dependencies of other dependencySets&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-579] - Dependency-filename appended as subdirectory&#010;of outputDirectory of dependencySet when unpackOptions/filtered = true&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-582] - Plugin omits transitive runtime dependencies&#010;where artifact is present with test-scope in current project&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-619] - Configurations of different &lt;dependencySet&gt;s&#010;influence each other&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-640] - Artifact data added to path when lineEnding&#010;tag set in dependencySet&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-672] - unpack adds the name of the artifact in case&#010;of filtered unpack&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-691] - dependencySet with filtered option has&#010;differents behaviors&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-701] - class AddDependencySetsTask doesn't re-unpack&#010;contents of unpacked SNAPSHOT artifacts&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-722] - Assembly with filters fails on Version 2.5&#010;with NoSuchElementException and then IOException (This archives&#010;contains unclosed entries) on clean up&#010;    * [MASSEMBLY-727] - Implied dependencysets have incorrect outputfilemapping&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010; [ANN] Apache Maven Surefire Plugin 2.18 Released  
Date  :-
Sat, 08 Nov 2014 12:08:42 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache&#010;Maven Surefire Plugin, version 2.18&#010;&#010;The release contains a number of bug fixes, and introduces an option to&#010;automatically rerun failing tests, including proper reporting on the&#010;console and in the XML reports for the individual runs.&#010;Again we received some much appreciated contributions from the community in&#010;form of bug reports, bug fixes and patches for new features. Thank you and&#010;keep 'em coming!&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.&#010;plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-surefire-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.18&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;or for failsafe:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-failsafe-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.18&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Surefire - Version 2.18&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-649] - Might be impossible to have empty strings in&#010;systemPropertyVariables element&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-941] - TESTS header printed twice when forkMode is always&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-963] - Unable to set empty environment variables&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1023] - Report generation fails with&#010;StringIndexOutOfBoundsException&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1028] - Unable to run single test (junit)&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1069] - Typo in alwaysGenerateSurefireReport doc:&#010;"Defaulyts"&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1072] - Duplicate example of commandline in run single test&#010;documentation&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1075] - Addresses to documented mailing lists in Maven site&#010;dead&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1077] - NPE problem will happen if you set testng status to&#010;fail at afterInvocation method&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1078] - Failure running forked mode with TestNG test suites&#010;defined via XML files&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1080] - Use parallel and fork together run some tests&#010;multiple times&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1081] - Doc claims parallel is TestNG only, but rest of doc&#010;implies junit works, too.&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1088] - When test fail during initialization the test&#010;execution time can result in a large negative number.&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1090] - NPE in SmartStacktraceParser if&#010;Thread.contextCassLoader is null&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1091] - IOException when test with much output prints in&#010;@After / @AfterClass - possible haning processes&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1104] - Internal Maven Surefire IT tests fail with Maven&#010;3.2.x&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [SUREFIRE-1053] - Suppress warning message if file.encoding is set&#010;using argLine&#010; Hi Kevin,&#010;&#010;to download a an file from somewhere you could use the &#010;wagon-maven-plugin like this:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;   &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;   &lt;artifactId&gt;wagon-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;   &lt;version&gt;1.0-beta-5&lt;/version&gt;&#010;   &lt;executions&gt;&#010;     &lt;execution&gt;&#010;       &lt;id&gt;download-test-data&lt;/id&gt;&#010;       &lt;phase&gt;prepare-package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;       &lt;goals&gt;&#010;         &lt;goal&gt;download-single&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;       &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;       &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;         &lt;url&gt;http://archive.apache.org/dist/abdera/1.1.2/&lt;/url&gt;&#010;         &lt;fromFile&gt;apache-abdera-1.1.2-src.tar.gz&lt;/fromFile&gt;&#010;         &lt;toDir&gt;${project.build.directory}/environment/qa&lt;/toDir&gt;&#010;       &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;     &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;   &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;For unpacking of the tar.gz you&#010;On 11/8/14 7:40 PM, Kevin Burton wrote:&#010;&gt; I’m trying to build .debs using jdeb and maven for various projects.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; For example, there is no .deb for spark.  So I’m just taking the tar.gz and&#010;&gt; making a deb that installs to /usr/share/apache-spark.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The problem is I don’t want to put the full binary into git as it’s about&#010;&gt; 200MB.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I’d rather have the build fetch the tar.gz directly from Apache during the&#010;&gt; build, untar it, then build the deb from the output.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Is there and way to do this or should I just write a bash script which uses&#010;&gt; wget to fetch the URL?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Sign and deploy a pom-only artifact to maven central  
Date  :-
Sun, 09 Nov 2014 11:50:44 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I'm trying to introduce a common parent pom for my projects. So I have &#010;created a maven artifact which only consists of that pom.xml and no &#010;further sources, resources or whatsoever. On a "normal" project, upon &#010;deploying, a "artifactId-version.pom" and corresponding .asc is created &#010;within the target folder.&#010;&#010;However, on my pom-only project, there is no signed output for the pom &#010;file and thus deploying to maven central fails (staging actually works, &#010;but the staging repo can not be closed because the central sync &#010;requirement "Signature Validation" fails).&#010;&#010;I'm basically following the guide here:&#010;http://central.sonatype.org/pages/apache-maven.html&#010;for deploying to maven central.&#010;&#010;How can I force a signed output for the pom file?&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Regards&#010;Simon&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Robert Metzger &lt;rmetz...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Change dependency version through property  
Date  :-
Fri, 14 Nov 2014 14:23:56 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I'm a developer at the Apache Flink (incubating) project. I'm trying to&#010;pass the version of a dependency using a property from the command line to&#010;the binary build. But it seems that the version I've set is not respected&#010;everywhere.&#010;&#010;&#010;We have the following setup:&#010;- flink-parent&#010;   - flink-core&#010;   - ... more modules ...&#010;   - flink-yarn&#010;   - flink-dist&#010;&#010;The "flink-yarn" module (and others) have dependencies to Apache Hadoop. We&#010;have a property (called hadoop.version) to have one place for setting the&#010;Hadoop version. The default Hadoop version 2.2.0.&#010;&#010;The "flink-dist" module is creating the binary release for Flink. It is&#010;using the maven-assembly-plugin for that. All jars we depend on are placed&#010;in the "lib" directory.&#010;The "flink-dist" module has most of our modules (also the flink-yarn)&#010;module as a dependency so that we can use the modules in the assembly.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;What I'm trying to do is building Flink for a different Hadoop version, say&#010;"2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2". Therefore, I'm passing this version as&#010;"-Dhadoop.version=2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2".&#010;&#010;However, some files from Hadoop "2.2.0" end up in the "lib" directory.&#010;&#010;mvn dependency:tree reveals for "flink-dist":&#010;&#010;[INFO] +- org.apache.flink:flink-yarn:jar:0.8-incubating-SNAPSHOT:compile&#010;[INFO] |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-client:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;[INFO] |  |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-api:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;[INFO] |  |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-common:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;&#010;however, for "flink-yarn" the versions are correct:&#010;&#010;[INFO] +-&#010;org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-client:jar:2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2:compile&#010;[INFO] |  +- commons-logging:commons-logging:jar:1.1.3:compile&#010;[INFO] |  +- commons-lang:commons-lang:jar:2.6:compile&#010;&#010;Here is the full dependency:tree output:&#010;https://gist.github.com/rmetzger/70c5f35d4cfd06a91169&#010;&#010;&#010;How can I create builds for different Hadoop versions using Maven?&#010;&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Ron Wheeler &lt;rwhee...@artifact-software.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Change dependency version through property  
Date  :-
Fri, 14 Nov 2014 15:29:00 GMT  
contents:- 
You are asking the right question in the right forum.&#010;&#010;I can give you a bit of background that describes why you are having &#010;trouble with Maven.&#010;&#010;Maven has a mind of its own.&#010;At the core of its belief system is the basic principle that anyone &#010;should be able to go to your SCM, download some version of your sources &#010;and pom files and tell Maven to build the project and get exactly what &#010;you got when you did this.&#010;Allowing command line arguments to affect the build would violate Maven &#010;core beliefs&#010;&#010;Maven will fight any attempt to bend or break its resolve in this regard.&#010;The phrase "Resistence if futile!" comes up in this forum from time to time.&#010;&#010;Given that you can't do what you want, here are some ideas that might &#010;give you some better ideas for a solution.&#010;1) Does any of your code actually care at compile time what version of &#010;Hadoop it builds with? If not, you have a run-time issue not really a &#010;build issue.&#010;2) Is you problem really one of testing with different Hadoop versions? &#010;In that case, you can just build your jar with a "typical/generic"Hadoop &#010;&lt;scope&gt;provided&lt;/scope&gt; and use that jar with different combinations of &#010;Hadoop versions in various test environments to certify that it works.&#010;2) What if a neutral version of Hadoop was used at compile time but not &#010;included in your jar &lt;scope&gt;provided&lt;/scope&gt;and a different one was used &#010;at run-time, would your application run. If so, you could distribute &#010;your application without Hadoop and let the user add their own Hadoop &#010;jars to the classpath at run-time.&#010;3) Are you going to distribute your software with an installer that &#010;would allow you to build various versions of your installer (or add &#010;options to your installer) to install the "right" Hadoop as part of the &#010;installation.&#010;&#010;I know that these are not the answers that you wanted or expected but I &#010;hope it gives you some ideas that moves you forward.&#010;&#010;&#010;On 14/11/2014 9:23 AM, Robert Metzger wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm a developer at the Apache Flink (incubating) project. I'm trying to&#010;&gt; pass the version of a dependency using a property from the command line to&#010;&gt; the binary build. But it seems that the version I've set is not respected&#010;&gt; everywhere.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We have the following setup:&#010;&gt; - flink-parent&#010;&gt;     - flink-core&#010;&gt;     - ... more modules ...&#010;&gt;     - flink-yarn&#010;&gt;     - flink-dist&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The "flink-yarn" module (and others) have dependencies to Apache Hadoop. We&#010;&gt; have a property (called hadoop.version) to have one place for setting the&#010;&gt; Hadoop version. The default Hadoop version 2.2.0.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The "flink-dist" module is creating the binary release for Flink. It is&#010;&gt; using the maven-assembly-plugin for that. All jars we depend on are placed&#010;&gt; in the "lib" directory.&#010;&gt; The "flink-dist" module has most of our modules (also the flink-yarn)&#010;&gt; module as a dependency so that we can use the modules in the assembly.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What I'm trying to do is building Flink for a different Hadoop version, say&#010;&gt; "2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2". Therefore, I'm passing this version as&#010;&gt; "-Dhadoop.version=2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2".&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; However, some files from Hadoop "2.2.0" end up in the "lib" directory.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; mvn dependency:tree reveals for "flink-dist":&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [INFO] +- org.apache.flink:flink-yarn:jar:0.8-incubating-SNAPSHOT:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-client:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-api:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-common:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; however, for "flink-yarn" the versions are correct:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [INFO] +-&#010;&gt; org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-client:jar:2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  +- commons-logging:commons-logging:jar:1.1.3:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  +- commons-lang:commons-lang:jar:2.6:compile&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Here is the full dependency:tree output:&#010;&gt; https://gist.github.com/rmetzger/70c5f35d4cfd06a91169&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; How can I create builds for different Hadoop versions using Maven?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi Robert,&#010;&#010;Robert Metzger wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I'm a developer at the Apache Flink (incubating) project. I'm trying to&#010;&gt; pass the version of a dependency using a property from the command line to&#010;&gt; the binary build. But it seems that the version I've set is not respected&#010;&gt; everywhere.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; We have the following setup:&#010;&gt; - flink-parent&#010;&gt;    - flink-core&#010;&gt;    - ... more modules ...&#010;&gt;    - flink-yarn&#010;&gt;    - flink-dist&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; The "flink-yarn" module (and others) have dependencies to Apache Hadoop.&#010;&gt; We have a property (called hadoop.version) to have one place for setting&#010;&gt; the Hadoop version. The default Hadoop version 2.2.0.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; The "flink-dist" module is creating the binary release for Flink. It is&#010;&gt; using the maven-assembly-plugin for that. All jars we depend on are placed&#010;&gt; in the "lib" directory.&#010;&gt; The "flink-dist" module has most of our modules (also the flink-yarn)&#010;&gt; module as a dependency so that we can use the modules in the assembly.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; What I'm trying to do is building Flink for a different Hadoop version,&#010;&gt; say "2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2". Therefore, I'm passing this version as&#010;&gt; "-Dhadoop.version=2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2".&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; However, some files from Hadoop "2.2.0" end up in the "lib" directory.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; mvn dependency:tree reveals for "flink-dist":&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; [INFO] +- org.apache.flink:flink-yarn:jar:0.8-incubating-SNAPSHOT:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-client:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-api:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  |  +- org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-common:jar:2.2.0:compile&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; however, for "flink-yarn" the versions are correct:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; [INFO] +-&#010;&gt; org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-yarn-client:jar:2.2.0-cdh5.0.0-beta-2:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  +- commons-logging:commons-logging:jar:1.1.3:compile&#010;&gt; [INFO] |  +- commons-lang:commons-lang:jar:2.6:compile&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Here is the full dependency:tree output:&#010;&gt; https://gist.github.com/rmetzger/70c5f35d4cfd06a91169&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; How can I create builds for different Hadoop versions using Maven?&#010;&#010;General rule:&#010;- don't use a version tag for direct dependencies&#010;- use a common parent for all modules with&#010;  - a dependency management section for any dependency you want to control&#010;  - use properties for these versions&#010;&#010;These properties can be overwritten from command line or setting the &#010;property again explicitly in a module.&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

[ANN] Apache Maven Toolchains Plugin 1.1 Released  
Date  :-
Sat, 15 Nov 2014 00:55:38 GMT  
contents:- 
The Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache Maven &#010;Toolchains Plugin, version 1.1&#010;&#010;The Toolchains Plugins allows to share configuration across plugins. For &#010;example to make sure the plugins like compiler, surefire, javadoc, webstart &#010;etc. all use the same JDK for execution.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-toolchains-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-toolchains-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;1.1&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Apache Maven Toolchains Plugin - Version 1.1&#010;&#010;Bug&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-6] Cannot create custom toolchain type&#010;&#010;Improvement&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-11] Double check toolchain type to protect against core bug &#010;MNG-5716&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-10] Improve plugin output&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-1] Document how to create new toolchains&#010;&#010;Task&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-9] Upgrade to Maven 2.2.1 compatiblity&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-8] improve code and javadoc&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-7] add an IT to check that the plugin works as expected&#010;* [MTOOLCHAINS-4] use maven-plugin-tools' java 5 annotations&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Maven team&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

no, there is no feature like this: in general, toolchains configuration is static&#010;&#010;in your case, using a variable like this makes the configuration ambiguous, since the jdk&#010;1.6 and 1.7 point to the same location: I'm not sur it's a good idea.&#010;But perhaps it can be useful to others.&#010;&#010;We are working on toolchains enhancements for next Maven version [1]&#010;Please open a Jira issue to track the feature request and discussion about doing it or not&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Hervé&#010;&#010;[1] http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MNG-3891&#010;&#010;----- Mail original -----&#010;De: "Bruce Albrecht" &lt;bruce@zuhause.org&gt;&#010;À: "Maven Users List" &lt;users@maven.apache.org&gt;&#010;Envoyé: Samedi 15 Novembre 2014 19:59:49&#010;Objet: Re: [ANN] Apache Maven Toolchains Plugin 1.1 Released&#010;&#010;Can the toolchain.xml file contain Maven properties including references&#010;to system environment variables using ${env.VARIABLE}? The Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Maven&#010;Repository Builder shared library, version 1.0&#010;&#010;This library is used primarily to assemble Maven repository directory&#010;structures based on the dependencies of a project or set of projects,&#010;and provides the implementation for the &lt;repositories/&gt; section of&#010;the Maven Assembly Plugin assembly descriptor.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/shared/maven-repository-builder/&#010;&#010;You can use the repository builder library in your own project by&#010;adding the following dependency:&#010;&#010;&lt;dependency&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.shared&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-repository-builder&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;1.0&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hello,&#010;&#010;just another viewpoint: put your overview documents with a large number&#010;of @links into the package description. This is the best you can do&#010;with Javadoc. It is not rerally a good replacement for colaterals like&#010;Tutorials or Walk-Throughs (and sample code).&#010;&#010;Gruss&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;&#010;Am Sun, 16 Nov 2014 11:28:22&#010;-0800 schrieb Kevin Burton &lt;burton@spinn3r.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; This is slightly off topic so I apologize.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Javadoc is great for the developer but the main problem is that&#010;&gt; important documents can be hidden in a sea of classes.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; My Javadoc tends to have say 20-40 important documents on the design&#010;&gt; of a system but the rest of the Javadoc just tends to have an&#010;&gt; overview.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I’d like a way to organize it more as a book, maybe even by the&#010;&gt; length of the documentation instead of being organized as a table of&#010;&gt; contents.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; This way my ops guys and other members of the team can find the&#010;&gt; documentation they’re looking for and not necessarily how a specific&#010;&gt; component behaves.&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi,&#010;The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of Apache&#010;Maven Wagon 2.8.&#010;Apache Maven Wagon is a transport abstraction that is used in Maven's&#010;artifact and repository handling code.&#010;&#010;Web site: http://maven.apache.org/wagon/&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Wagon - Version 2.8&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [WAGON-416] - Lightweight HTTP Wagon doesn't set&#010;Proxy-Authorization header&#010;    * [WAGON-422] - HTTP wagon AuthScope is not definable from settings&#010;&#010;&#010;Have fun&#010;-- &#010;The Apache Maven Team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;Maven Wagon 2.7 (and presumably 2.8) fixes a bug in Maven related to&#010;client-side SSL certificates by upgrading its dependencies to a newer&#010;version of Apache HttpComponents httpclient. This is great, because it&#010;is now possible to use Maven with a private artefact repository&#010;secured with two-way SSL verification.&#010;&#010;However Apache Maven itself still depends on Wagon 2.6, at least in&#010;the stable release and on its git master. When might there be a stable&#010;Maven release depending on Maven Wagon 2.7 or 2.8?&#010;&#010;2014-11-17 1:15 GMT+01:00 Olivier Lamy &lt;olamy@apache.org&gt;:&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of Apache&#010;&gt; Maven Wagon 2.8.&#010;&gt; Apache Maven Wagon is a transport abstraction that is used in Maven's&#010;&gt; artifact and repository handling code.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Web site: http://maven.apache.org/wagon/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Release Notes - Maven Wagon - Version 2.8&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ** Bug&#010;&gt;     * [WAGON-416] - Lightweight HTTP Wagon doesn't set&#010;&gt; Proxy-Authorization header&#010;&gt;     * [WAGON-422] - HTTP wagon AuthScope is not definable from settings&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Have fun&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; The Apache Maven Team&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Kind regards,&#010;&#010;Jeroen Hoek&#010;Lable&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Jason van Zyl &lt;ja...@takari.io&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: API-s/Maven plugins for generation of REST API documentation  
Date  :-
Tue, 18 Nov 2014 14:32:33 GMT  
contents:- 
I am a long time user of Swagger and am fairly happy with it.&#010;&#010;I immediately ruled out API Blueprints because there's no Java implementation. I use Ruby&#010;everyday (almost) but I still find using Java and Ruby together sometimes difficult even with&#010;the presence of JRuby.&#010;&#010;RAML popped up a while ago and formed a working group and this spurred some activity on the&#010;Swagger side, they are both funded efforts.&#010;&#010;Swagger has some interesting associated tools, the only drawback for me personally is much&#010;of this is written in Scala. I'm indifferent to Scala, if people are productive with it that's&#010;great, but I don't want to learn another Java-like language to use/extend a tool. The area&#010;where this affected me is that I wanted to dynamically generate the Swagger documents from&#010;JAXRS annotations at runtime but this means you have to include the Scala runtime which was&#010;a showstopper for my project. But to use the Javascript console you only need to produce the&#010;documents. You can use the use the swagger doclet[1] to produce the document from JAXRS annotation,&#010;create the document manually, or use whatever other means. I just wrote a small tool to scan&#010;the annotations and produce the document. But once you have the document the console[2] is&#010;great and you can use all the nifty client generators which are very handy. Once the console&#010;is working the Javascript client is generated on the fly. The Javascript console is a straight&#010;forward Backbone application so it's fairly easy to augment/extend.&#010;&#010;The RAML tools look great and I have a lot of respect for the guys at MuleSoft but just haven't&#010;had time to play with it.&#010;&#010;[1]: https://github.com/ryankennedy/swagger-jaxrs-doclet&#010;[2]: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger-ui&#010;&#010;On Nov 17, 2014, at 11:08 PM, Jeff Jensen &lt;jeffjensen@upstairstechnology.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Some additional ones to consider:&#010;&gt; Swagger [0]&#010;&gt; API BluePrint [1]&#010;&gt; RAML [2]&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I find the most ecosystem around Swagger; seems the most popular. Nice list&#010;&gt; of integrations (see the link to Maven plugin) [3]&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; [0] http://swagger.io&#010;&gt; [1] http://apiblueprint.org&#010;&gt; [2] http://raml.org&#010;&gt; [3] https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger-spec#additional-libraries&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; On Mon, Nov 17, 2014 at 7:55 PM, Martin Todorov &lt;carlspring@gmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Perhaps this isn't the right mailing list, but it's partially&#010;&gt;&gt; Maven-related...&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; I've been wondering: are there some existing API-s and Maven plugins that&#010;&gt;&gt; can generate either of the following:&#010;&gt;&gt; a) Javadoc generators for REST API-s&#010;&gt;&gt; b) Markdown-styled documentation generators for REST API-s&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; I'm aware of Enunciate... Is that the only option, or are there any others&#010;&gt;&gt; that can be used with Maven plugins?&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Thanks in advance for any hints!&#010;&gt;&gt; Kind regards,&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Martin Todorov&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Jason&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------&#010;Jason van Zyl&#010;Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&#010;People develop abstractions by generalizing from concrete examples.&#010;Every attempt to determine the correct abstraction on paper without&#010;actually developing a running system is doomed to failure. No one&#010;is that smart. A framework is a resuable design, so you develop it by&#010;looking at the things it is supposed to be a design of. The more examples&#010;you look at, the more general your framework will be.&#010;&#010;  -- Ralph Johnson &amp; Don Roberts, Patterns for Evolving Frameworks &#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

The Javascript console is a&#010;&gt; straight forward Backbone application so it's fairly easy to augment/extend.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The RAML tools look great and I have a lot of respect for the guys at&#010;&gt; MuleSoft but just haven't had time to play with it.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [1]: https://github.com/ryankennedy/swagger-jaxrs-doclet&#010;&gt; [2]: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger-ui&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Nov 17, 2014, at 11:08 PM, Jeff Jensen &lt;&#010;&gt; jeffjensen@upstairstechnology.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Some additional ones to consider:&#010;&gt; &gt; Swagger [0]&#010;&gt; &gt; API BluePrint [1]&#010;&gt; &gt; RAML [2]&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I find the most ecosystem around Swagger; seems the most popular. Nice&#010;&gt; list&#010;&gt; &gt; of integrations (see the link to Maven plugin) [3]&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; [0] http://swagger.io&#010;&gt; &gt; [1] http://apiblueprint.org&#010;&gt; &gt; [2] http://raml.org&#010;&gt; &gt; [3] https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger-spec#additional-libraries&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On Mon, Nov 17, 2014 at 7:55 PM, Martin Todorov &lt;carlspring@gmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Perhaps this isn't the right mailing list, but it's partially&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Maven-related...&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; I've been wondering: are there some existing API-s and Maven plugins&#010;&gt; that&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; can generate either of the following:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; a) Javadoc generators for REST API-s&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; b) Markdown-styled documentation generators for REST API-s&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; I'm aware of Enunciate... Is that the only option, or are there any&#010;&gt; others&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; that can be used with Maven plugins?&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Thanks in advance for any hints!&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Kind regards,&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; Martin Todorov&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Jason&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ----------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; Jason van Zyl&#010;&gt; Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;&gt; http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;&gt; http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; People develop abstractions by generalizing from concrete examples.&#010;&gt; Every attempt to determine the correct abstraction on paper without&#010;&gt; actually developing a running system is doomed to failure. No one&#010;&gt; is that smart. A framework is a resuable design, so you develop it by&#010;&gt; looking at the things it is supposed to be a design of. The more examples&#010;&gt; you look at, the more general your framework will be.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   -- Ralph Johnson &amp; Don Roberts, Patterns for Evolving Frameworks&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
Hello Fábio,&#010;&#010;As far as I know the SCM configuration is not used to download&#010;sources. It is used mainly to commit and tag your project; it is used&#010;by the Maven Release Plugin (for example).&#010;&#010;I suspect you want the source code available in an IDE?&#010;&#010;The Maven Source Plugin is what you probably want:&#010;https://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-source-plugin/&#010;&#010;You can add this:&#010;https://gist.github.com/jdhoek/a482c0958f5371f5ea6c&#010;… to your build-&gt;plugins section in the POM to generate the source jars.&#010;&#010;2014-11-19 18:49 GMT+01:00 Fábio Franco &lt;fabiofranco.php@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt; I thought using scm element in the pom I´d be able to download the&#010;&gt; project´s source from a super project that depends on the first project.&#010;&gt; Was I wrong? Producing and building against separate branches

Here is our scenario:&#010;&#010;We have our SCM trunk and a "release candidate" branch. We merge code into the "RC" branch&#010;when we want it to go into the next release.&#010;&#010;In the past everyone built against the RC branch artifacts. However, now we have two release&#010;cycles going at the same time and some people want to build against the RC branch and others&#010;want to build against the trunk. We also need to setup servers, etc with the proper artifacts.&#010;&#010;So, I think I need to produce two artifacts for each project: "project-version.jar" and "project-version-trunk.jar".&#010;This, I think is simple, I just set the &lt;finalName&gt; in the trunk profile.&#010;&#010;Now, how do I use these so that a user building under the "trunk" profile will only use artifacts&#010;with the new classifier?&#010;&#010;We have a parent POM, used everywhere, that defines all of our dependency management to insure&#010;everyone stays "on version" for all of our dependencies. Could I create a property in the&#010;"trunk" profile and then use that in our dependency  management? For example:&#010;&#010;&lt;profile&gt;&#010;                &lt;id&gt;trunk&lt;/id&gt;&#010;                &lt;build&gt;&#010;                                &lt;finalname&gt;${project.artifactId}-${project.version}-head&lt;finalName&gt;&#010;                &lt;/build&gt;&#010;                &lt;properties&gt;&#010;                                &lt;our.classifier&gt;head&lt;/our.classifier&gt; &lt;-- property&#010;to use in dependencies&#010;                &lt;/properties&gt;&#010;                ...&#010;&lt;/profile&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;                &lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;                                &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;                                                &lt;groupId&gt;com.ours&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;                                                &lt;artifactId&gt;project1&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                                                &lt;version&gt;${project.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;                                                &lt;classifier&gt;${our.classifier}&lt;/classifier&gt;&#010;&lt;-- use of the property (if the property DNE, or is blank, is that OK?&#010;                                &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;                                ...&#010;                &lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;This is just me using my limited understanding trying to figure out the solution - if there&#010;is a more appropriate way to do this please let me know&#010;&#010;&#010;Thanks&#010;scott&#010;&#010;&#010;

Re: Producing and building against separate branches

contents:- 
As no one else has jumped on this, I'd like to pass on some hints/pointers.&#010;They are based on my own experience and also my rule om thumb for Maven&#010;practice.&#010;&#010;First, never use the finalName. It will only affect the name of the locally&#010;produced artifact (typically in the target folder). It will not affect the&#010;artifact name in the Maven repo, which is what really matters. So using it&#010;will only give you a false feeling of a solution which will break sooner or&#010;later.&#010;&#010;Second, never use profiles. Well, profiles is simply the starting point to&#010;nightmares and very bad Maven solutions. There are many threads on this.&#010;Just stay away of them...:-)&#010;&#010;Third, classifiers are typically not something that you should use. There&#010;are some cases where they could be used, but try to stay away from them.&#010;&#010;Saying that, I think the solution for you is to have different versions if&#010;you want to differentiate the branches. Could be, for example, 1.0.0&#010;(-SNAPSHOT) for the RC branch and 1.1.0 (-SNAPSHOT) for trunk. I don't&#010;understand the point of having two RC branches though. Are they for the&#010;same release (version) or two different releases? If you, strangely I'd&#010;say, have two RC branches for the same "release" you should add some&#010;postfix to the version. For example 1.0.0 (-SNAPSHOT) and 1.0.0-EXTRACOOL&#010;(-SNAPSHOT).&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;On Thu, Nov 20, 2014 at 12:14 AM, Scott Klein &lt;Scott.Klein@goldenhour.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Here is our scenario:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We have our SCM trunk and a "release candidate" branch. We merge code into&#010;&gt; the "RC" branch when we want it to go into the next release.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In the past everyone built against the RC branch artifacts. However, now&#010;&gt; we have two release cycles going at the same time and some people want to&#010;&gt; build against the RC branch and others want to build against the trunk. We&#010;&gt; also need to setup servers, etc with the proper artifacts.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So, I think I need to produce two artifacts for each project:&#010;&gt; "project-version.jar" and "project-version-trunk.jar". This, I think is&#010;&gt; simple, I just set the &lt;finalName&gt; in the trunk profile.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Now, how do I use these so that a user building under the "trunk" profile&#010;&gt; will only use artifacts with the new classifier?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We have a parent POM, used everywhere, that defines all of our dependency&#010;&gt; management to insure everyone stays "on version" for all of our&#010;&gt; dependencies. Could I create a property in the "trunk" profile and then use&#010;&gt; that in our dependency  management? For example:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;profile&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;id&gt;trunk&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;build&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;finalname&gt;${project.artifactId}-${project.version}-head&lt;finalName&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;/build&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;properties&gt;&#010;&gt;                                 &lt;our.classifier&gt;head&lt;/our.classifier&gt; &lt;--&#010;&gt; property to use in dependencies&#010;&gt;                 &lt;/properties&gt;&#010;&gt;                 ...&#010;&gt; &lt;/profile&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;                                 &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;                                                 &lt;groupId&gt;com.ours&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;artifactId&gt;project1&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;version&gt;${project.version}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;classifier&gt;${our.classifier}&lt;/classifier&gt; &lt;-- use of the property (if&#010;the&#010;&gt; property DNE, or is blank, is that OK?&#010;&gt;                                 &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;                                 ...&#010;&gt;                 &lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;/dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; This is just me using my limited understanding trying to figure out the&#010;&gt; solution - if there is a more appropriate way to do this please let me know&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt; scott&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

[DISCUSS] Adopt Mr Couché-Tard as our mascot, change the logo font to Alte Haas Grotesk, change the colour letter to &quot;v&quot;  
Date  :-
Thu, 20 Nov 2014 10:49:52 GMT  
contents:- 
The closest thing to a mascot that we have is&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/images/maven-logo-2.gif&#010;"Arse on desk behind laptop while waiting for Maven to finish downloading&#010;the interwebs"&#010;&#010;I would like to call a vote in a couple of days to adopt M. Couché-Tard (my&#010;own creation) as our mascot&#010;&#010;http://people.apache.org/~stephenc/maven-logo-contest/maven-owl-5-large.png&#010;"M. Couché-Tard"&#010;&#010;In addition I am suggesting that we change the logo font to Alte Haas&#010;Grotesk Bold with italic applied by Inkscape&#010;&#010;I am also suggesting that we change the emphasis colour letter to the v...&#010;as in version... and we all know that Maven helps manage versions of&#010;things... versions are very important to Maven.&#010;&#010;The emphasis colour would be #cc0000 to match the scarf worn by "M.&#010;Couché-Tard"&#010;&#010;My proposal would be to make these changes as a single vote, i.e. not three&#010;separate votes, the vote would be for all these changes in one go... in&#010;order to avoid design by committee.&#010;&#010;Having said that, community is more important than a new logo or even&#010;having a mascot, so hence this discuss thread before actually calling a&#010;vote.&#010;&#010;This is something that not just the developers of Maven should have a say&#010;in... if we have a mascot and a refreshed logo we can use these as aid to&#010;help drive a site refresh that makes Maven easier to understand for&#010;newcomers and helps existing users find what they are looking for easier&#010;and faster.&#010;&#010;For anyone not following the dev list, here is my reasons for picking "M.&#010;Couché-Tard" as a mascot...&#010;&#010;The definition of a maven is "an expert or connoisseur"... in the context&#010;of Apache Maven, the idea is that Maven knows the conventions for different&#010;types of software projects and is an expert in applying those conventions.&#010;M. Couché-Tard is a wise fellow, sleeping-in while he waits for the&#010;interwebs to finish downloading... he may look cute but if crossed or used&#010;incorrectly he will bite a chunk off your hand... but do right by him and&#010;he will do right by you.&#010;&#010;So WDYT? should I just call the vote already or do people want to think it&#010;over a bit more!&#010;&#010;

Couché-Tard is a wise fellow, sleeping-in while he waits for the&#010;&gt;&gt; interwebs to finish downloading... he may look cute but if crossed or used&#010;&gt;&gt; incorrectly he will bite a chunk off your hand... but do right by him and&#010;&gt;&gt; he will do right by you.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; So WDYT? should I just call the vote already or do people want to think it&#010;&gt;&gt; over a bit more!&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; three&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; separate votes, the vote would be for all these changes in&#010;one&#010;&gt;&gt; go...&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; in&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; order to avoid design by committee.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Having said that, community is more important than a new logo&#010;or&#010;&gt;&gt; of Apache Maven, the idea is that Maven knows the conventions&#010;for&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; different&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; types of software projects and is an expert in applying those&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; conventions.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; My opinion on this:&#010;&#010;I do not like the connection between the owl and the word maven.&#010;While the owl stands for wisdom in the Greek culture as on the Greek &#010;euro coins, Maven is not of Greek origin. It is cleary of Hebrew/Jewish &#010;[1] origin. I see no connection here. I would rather see an old and wise &#010;man.&#010;&#010;I see no point on having 'v' in a different color, as if the word &#010;consists of two syllables. It is just a coincidence that the words &#010;'maven' and 'version' have/share the 'v' combination.&#010;&#010;Unfortunately, I have artistic talent, so I cannot come up with a decent &#010;vector graphic for an old and wise man :-(&#010;&#010;[1] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maven&#010;&#010;Michael&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;
